The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\\n39: //!   \\\"backtrace\\\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\\n46: //!\\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\\n56: //!\\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\\n59: //! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\\n60: //!\\n61: //! ### Implementation details\\n62: //!\\n63: //! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\\n64: //! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\\n65: //! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\\n66: //! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\\n67: //! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\\n68: //! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\\n69: //! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\\n70: //! aren't needed anymore.\\n71: \\n72: use std::cell::Cell;\\n73: use std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\\n74: use std::fmt::Debug;\\n75: use std::hash;\\n76: use std::marker::PhantomData;\\n77: \\n78: use thin_vec::ThinVec;\\n79: use tracing::debug;\\n80: \\n81: use crate::fx::{FxHashMap, FxHashSet};\\n82: \\n83: mod graphviz;\\n84: \\n85: #[cfg(test)]\\n86: mod tests;\\n87: \\n88: pub trait ForestObligation: Clone + Debug {\\n89:     type CacheKey: Clone + hash::Hash + Eq + Debug;\\n90: \\n91:     /// Converts this `ForestObligation` suitable for use as a cache key.\\n92:     /// If two distinct `ForestObligations`s return the same cache key,\\n93:     /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\\n94:     /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\\n95:     fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\\n96: }\\n97: \\n98: pub trait ObligationProcessor {\\n99:     type Obligation: ForestObligation;\\n100:     type Error: Debug;\\n101:     type OUT: OutcomeTrait<Obligation = Self::Obligation, Error = Error<Self::Obligation, Self::Error>>;\\n102: \\n103:     /// Implementations can provide a fast-path to obligation-processing\\n104:     /// by counting the prefix of the passed iterator for which\\n105:     /// `needs_process_obligation` would return false.\\n106:     fn skippable_obligations<'a>(\\n107:         &'a self,\\n108:         _it: impl Iterator<Item = &'a Self::Obligation>,\\n109:     ) -> usize {\\n110:         0\\n111:     }\\n112: \\n113:     fn needs_process_obligation(&self, _obligation: &Self::Obligation) -> bool;\\n114: \\n115:     fn process_obligation(\\n116:         &mut self,\\n117:         obligation: &mut Self::Obligation,\\n118:     ) -> ProcessResult<Self::Obligation, Self::Error>;\\n119: \\n120:     /// As we do the cycle check, we invoke this callback when we\\n121:     /// encounter an actual cycle. `cycle` is an iterator that starts\\n122:     /// at the start of the cycle in the stack and walks **toward the\\n123:     /// top**.\\n124:     ///\\n125:     /// In other words, if we had O1 which required O2 which required\\n126:     /// O3 which required O1, we would give an iterator yielding O1,\\n127:     /// O2, O3 (O1 is not yielded twice).\\n128:     fn process_backedge<'c, I>(\\n129:         &mut self,\\n130:         cycle: I,\\n131:         _marker: PhantomData<&'c Self::Obligation>,\\n132:     ) -> Result<(), Self::Error>\\n133:     where\\n134:         I: Clone + Iterator<Item = &'c Self::Obligation>;\\n135: }\\n136: \\n137: /// The result type used by `process_obligation`.\\n138: // `repr(C)` In between calls to [Self::process_obligations],\\n154:     /// this list only contains nodes in the `Pending` or `Waiting` state.\\n155:     ///\\n156:     /// `usize` indices are used here and throughout this module, rather than\\n157:     /// [`rustc_index::newtype_index!`] indices, because this code is hot enough\\n158:     /// that the `u32`-to-`usize` conversions that would be required are\\n159:     /// significant, and space considerations are not important.\\n160:     nodes: Vec<Node<O>>,\\n161: \\n162:     /// A cache of predicates that have been successfully completed.\\n163:     done_cache: FxHashSet<O::CacheKey>,\\n164: \\n165:     /// A cache of the nodes in `nodes`, indexed by predicate. Unfortunately,\\n166:     /// its contents are not guaranteed to match those of `nodes`. See the\\n167:     /// comments in `Self::process_obligation` for details.\\n168:     active_cache: FxHashMap<O::CacheKey, usize>,\\n169: \\n170:     /// A vector reused in [Self::compress()] and [Self::find_cycles_from_node()],\\n171:     /// to avoid allocating new vectors.\\n172:     reused_node_vec: Vec<usize>,\\n173: \\n174:     obligation_tree_id_generator: ObligationTreeIdGenerator,\\n175: \\n176:     /// Per tree error cache. They\\n192:     /// must all be in a non-pending state.\\n193:     dependents: Vec<usize>,\\n194: \\n195:     /// If true, `dependents[0]` points to a \\\"parent\\\" node, which requires\\n196:     /// special treatment upon error but is otherwise treated the same.\\n197:     /// (It would be more idiomatic to store the parent node in a separate\\n198:     /// `Option<usize>` field, but that slows down the common case of\\n199:     /// iterating over the parent and other descendants together.)\\n200:     has_parent: bool,\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs%3FL1-200\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"48cda48c-3bb5-4bc4-b7f3-99537387eefa","uuid":"552dedc4-f70a-4d10-8e36-c45cf2de1124","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! They\\n192:     /// must all be in a non-pending state.\\n193:     dependents: Vec<usize>,\\n194: \\n195:     /// If true, `dependents[0]` points to a \\\"parent\\\" node, which requires\\n196:     /// special treatment upon error but is otherwise treated the same.\\n197:     /// (It would be more idiomatic to store the parent node in a separate\\n198:     /// `Option<usize>` field, but that slows down the common case of\\n199:     /// iterating over the parent and other descendants together.)\\n200:     has_parent: bool,\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs%3FL1-200\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n14: //!\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n39: //!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\n43: //!\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\n46: //!\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n56: //!\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n59: //! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n60: //!\n61: //! ### Implementation details\n62: //!\n63: //! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n64: //! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n65: //! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n66: //! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n67: //! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n68: //! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\n69: //! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\n70: //! aren't needed anymore.\n71: \n72: use std::cell::Cell;\n73: use std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\n74: use std::fmt::Debug;\n75: use std::hash;\n76: use std::marker::PhantomData;\n77: \n78: use thin_vec::ThinVec;\n79: use tracing::debug;\n80: \n81: use crate::fx::{FxHashMap, FxHashSet};\n82: \n83: mod graphviz;\n84: \n85: #[cfg(test)]\n86: mod tests;\n87: \n88: pub trait ForestObligation: Clone + Debug {\n89:     type CacheKey: Clone + hash::Hash + Eq + Debug;\n90: \n91:     /// Converts this `ForestObligation` suitable for use as a cache key.\n92:     /// If two distinct `ForestObligations`s return the same cache key,\n93:     /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\n94:     /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\n95:     fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\n96: }\n97: \n98: pub trait ObligationProcessor {\n99:     type Obligation: ForestObligation;\n100:     type Error: Debug;\n101:     type OUT: OutcomeTrait<Obligation = Self::Obligation, Error = Error<Self::Obligation, Self::Error>>;\n102: \n103:     /// Implementations can provide a fast-path to obligation-processing\n104:     /// by counting the prefix of the passed iterator for which\n105:     /// `needs_process_obligation` would return false.\n106:     fn skippable_obligations<'a>(\n107:         &'a self,\n108:         _it: impl Iterator<Item = &'a Self::Obligation>,\n109:     ) -> usize {\n110:         0\n111:     }\n112: \n113:     fn needs_process_obligation(&self, _obligation: &Self::Obligation) -> bool;\n114: \n115:     fn process_obligation(\n116:         &mut self,\n117:         obligation: &mut Self::Obligation,\n118:     ) -> ProcessResult<Self::Obligation, Self::Error>;\n119: \n120:     /// As we do the cycle check, we invoke this callback when we\n121:     /// encounter an actual cycle. `cycle` is an iterator that starts\n122:     /// at the start of the cycle in the stack and walks **toward the\n123:     /// top**.\n124:     ///\n125:     /// In other words, if we had O1 which required O2 which required\n126:     /// O3 which required O1, we would give an iterator yielding O1,\n127:     /// O2, O3 (O1 is not yielded twice).\n128:     fn process_backedge<'c, I>(\n129:         &mut self,\n130:         cycle: I,\n131:         _marker: PhantomData<&'c Self::Obligation>,\n132:     ) -> Result<(), Self::Error>\n133:     where\n134:         I: Clone + Iterator<Item = &'c Self::Obligation>;\n135: }\n136: \n137: /// The result type used by `process_obligation`.\n138: // `repr(C)` to inhibit the niche filling optimization. Otherwise, the `match` appearing\n139: // in `process_obligations` is significantly slower, which can substantially affect\n140: // benchmarks like `rustc-perf`'s inflate and keccak.\n141: #[repr(C)]\n142: #[derive(Debug)]\n143: pub enum ProcessResult<O, E> {\n144:     Unchanged,\n145:     Changed(ThinVec<O>),\n146:     Error(E),\n147: }\n148: \n149: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Debug)]\n150: struct ObligationTreeId(usize);\n151: \n152: pub struct ObligationForest<O: ForestObligation> {\n153:     /// The list of obligations. In between calls to [Self::process_obligations],\n154:     /// this list only contains nodes in the `Pending` or `Waiting` state.\n155:     ///\n156:     /// `usize` indices are used here and throughout this module, rather than\n157:     /// [`rustc_index::newtype_index!`] indices, because this code is hot enough\n158:     /// that the `u32`-to-`usize` conversions that would be required are\n159:     /// significant, and space considerations are not important.\n160:     nodes: Vec<Node<O>>,\n161: \n162:     /// A cache of predicates that have been successfully completed.\n163:     done_cache: FxHashSet<O::CacheKey>,\n164: \n165:     /// A cache of the nodes in `nodes`, indexed by predicate. Unfortunately,\n166:     /// its contents are not guaranteed to match those of `nodes`. See the\n167:     /// comments in `Self::process_obligation` for details.\n168:     active_cache: FxHashMap<O::CacheKey, usize>,\n169: \n170:     /// A vector reused in [Self::compress()] and [Self::find_cycles_from_node()],\n171:     /// to avoid allocating new vectors.\n172:     reused_node_vec: Vec<usize>,\n173: \n174:     obligation_tree_id_generator: ObligationTreeIdGenerator,\n175: \n176:     /// Per tree error cache. This does end up as truly\\n45:             // ambiguous in most cases anyway.\\n46:             //\\n47:             // Take the fast path out - this also improves\\n48:             // performance by preventing assemble_candidates_from_impls from\\n49:             // matching every impl for this trait.\\n50:             return Ok(SelectionCandidateSet { vec: vec![], ambiguous: true });\\n51:         }\\n52: \\n53:         let mut candidates = SelectionCandidateSet { vec: Vec::new(), ambiguous: false };\\n54: \\n55:         // Negative trait predicates have different rules than positive trait predicates.\\n56:         if obligation.polarity() == ty::PredicatePolarity::Negative {\\n57:             self.assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias(obligation, &mut candidates);\\n58:             self.assemble_candidates_from_impls(obligation, &mut candidates);\\n59:             self.assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds(stack, &mut candidates)?;\\n60:         } else {\\n61:             self.assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias(obligation, &mut candidates);\\n62: \\n63:             // Other bounds. Consider both in-scope bounds from fn decl\\n64:             // and applicable impls. There is a certain set of precedence rules here.\\n65:             let def_id = obligation.predicate.def_id();\\n66:             let tcx = self.tcx();\\n67: \\n68:             let lang_item = tcx.as_lang_item(def_id);\\n69:             match lang_item {\\n70:                 Some(LangItem::Copy | LangItem::Clone | LangItem::TrivialClone) => {\\n71: and enums.\\n75:                     self.assemble_candidates_from_impls(obligation, &mut candidates);\\n76: \\n77:                     // For other types, we'll use the builtin rules.\\n78:                     self.assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate(\\n79:                         obligation.predicate.self_ty().skip_binder(),\\n80:                         &mut candidates,\\n81:                     );\\n82:                 }\\n83:                 Some(LangItem::DiscriminantKind) => {\\n84:                     // `DiscriminantKind` is automatically implemented for every type.\\n85:                     candidates.vec.push(BuiltinCandidate);\\n86:                 }\\n87:                 Some(LangItem::PointeeTrait) => {\\n88:                     // `Pointee` is automatically implemented for every type.\\n89:                     candidates.vec.push(BuiltinCandidate);\\n90:                 }\\n91:                 Some(LangItem::Sized) => {\\n92:                     self.assemble_builtin_sized_candidate(\\n93:                         obligation.predicate.self_ty().skip_binder(),\\n94:                         &mut candidates,\\n95: rustc_middle::ty::{self, InferConst, Ty, TyCtxt};\n6: use tracing::instrument;\n7: \n8: /// A type \"A\" *matches* \"B\" if the fresh types in B could be\n9: /// instantiated with values so as to make it equal to A. Matching is\n10: /// intended to be used only on freshened types, and it basically\n11: /// indicates if the non-freshened versions of A and B could have been\n12: /// unified.\n13: ///\n14: /// It is only an approximation. If it yields false, unification would\n15: /// definitely fail, but a true result doesn't mean unification would\n16: /// succeed. This is because we don't track the \"side-constraints\" on\n17: /// type variables, nor do we track if the same freshened type appears\n18: /// more than once. To some extent these approximations could be\n19: /// fixed, given effort.\n20: ///\n21: /// Like subtyping, matching is really a binary relation, so the only\n22: /// important thing about the result is Ok/Err. Also, matching never\n23: /// affects any type variables or unification state.\n24: pub(crate) struct MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx> {\n25:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n26: }\n27: \n28: impl<'tcx> Ty<'tcx>, b: Ty<'tcx>) -> RelateResult<'tcx, Ty<'tcx>> {\n60:         if a == b {\n61:             return Ok(a);\n62:         }\n63: \n64:         match (a.kind(), b.kind()) {\n65:             (\n66:                 _,\n67:                 &ty::Infer(ty::FreshTy(_))\n68:                 | &ty::Infer(ty::FreshIntTy(_))\n69:                 | &ty::Infer(ty::FreshFloatTy(_)),\n70:             ) => (&ty::Error(guar), _) | (_, &ty::Error(guar)) => Ok(Ty::new_error(self.cx(), guar)),\n77: \n78:             _ => structurally_relate_tys(self, a, b),\n79:         }\n80:     }\n81: \n82:     #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n83:     fn consts(\n84:         &mut self,\n85:         a: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n86:         b: ty::Const<'tcx>,\n87:     ) -> RelateResult<'tcx,   }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Rust Trait Obligation Fulfillment Chain\\n\\n### Overview\\nThe Rust trait solver fulfills trait obligations through a hierarchical system centered on the **ObligationForest** data structure, which manages the forest of pending trait obligations. The chain represents the old (traditional) trait solver architecture, with a modern new solver implementation alongside it.\\n\\n### Core Components\\n\\n#### 1. ObligationForest (rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)\\nThe **ObligationForest** is the fundamental data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It:\\n- Maintains a forest of obligation nodes, each with state (Pending, Waiting, Success, Error)\\n- Implements obligation dependency tracking with parent-child relationships\\n- Processes obligations via the `ObligationProcessor` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:268)\\n- Returns outcomes containing completed obligations and errors\\n- Caches processed results to avoid duplicate work\\n\\nThe forest uses three core result types defined by `ProcessResult<O, E>`:\\n- `Unchanged`: Ambiguous result, obligation stalled on type inference\\n- `Changed(Vec<O>)`: Obligation satisfied with subobligations\\n- `Error(E)`: Obligation failed\\n\\n#### 2. FulfillmentContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:61-104)\\nThe **FulfillmentContext** is the old trait solver's main context that manages trait fulfillment:\\n- Wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implements the `TraitEngine` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs:136)\\n- Registers obligations via `register_predicate_obligation()`\\n- Processes obligations through the `select()` method which invokes `FulfillProcessor`\\n- Snapshot-aware to ensure correct context usage\\n\\n#### 3. FulfillProcessor (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:252-450)\\nThe **FulfillProcessor** implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait and:\\n- Processes each obligation in the forest by invoking trait selection\\n- Implements `needs_process_obligation()` with optimizations checking stalled inference variables\\n- Calls `SelectionContext.select()` for each obligation\\n- Generates sub-obligations from confirmed candidates\\n- Converts solver errors to fulfillment errors\\n\\n#### 4. SelectionContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs:104-126)\\nThe **SelectionContext** is the central context for trait candidate selection:\\n- Maintains inference context and freshener for trait predicates\\n- Tracks intercrate ambiguity causes for coherence checking\\n- Implements the selection algorithm via `select()` and `candidate_from_obligation()`\\n- Manages trait obligation stacks to detect cycles\\n- Caches selection results for performance\\n\\n#### 5. Candidate Assembly (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs:25-100)\\nThe **assemble_candidates()** method:\\n- Collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation\\n- Sources candidates from:\\n  - Trait aliases\\n  - User-defined impl blocks\\n  - Where-clause bounds\\n  - Built-in traits (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n  - Projection predicates\\n- Returns a `SelectionCandidateSet` with definite and ambiguous candidates\\n\\n#### 6. Confirmation (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs:32-100)\\nThe **confirm_candidate()** method:\\n- Verifies that a selected candidate actually applies to the obligation\\n- Unifies trait reference type parameters\\n- Generates nested obligations based on the candidate type:\\n  - `ImplCandidate`: Calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` to generate where-clause obligations\\n  - `ParamCandidate`: Generates obligations from where-clause bounds\\n  - `BuiltinCandidate`: No nested obligations\\n  - `ObjectCandidate`, `ClosureCandidate`, etc.: Generate type-specific obligations\\n- Returns an `ImplSource` representing the selected implementation\\n\\n#### 7. Impl Matching (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs:24-117)\\nThe **MatchAgainstFreshVars** structure:\\n- Implements the `TypeRelation` trait to match types against fresh type variables\\n- Used to check if an impl's trait reference matches an obligation\\n- Approximates whether unification would succeed\\n- Returns Ok if match succeeds, Err if it fails\\n\\n#### 8. TraitEngine & ObligationCtxt (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs)\\nThe **TraitEngine** trait defines:\\n- `register_predicate_obligation()`: Adds obligations to the engine\\n- `try_evaluate_obligations()`: Processes pending obligations\\n- `report_fulfillment_errors()`: Reports errors for unfulfilled obligations\\n\\nThe **ObligationCtxt** provides a simpler API wrapper around TraitEngine.\\n\\n#### 9. Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/)\\nError reporting occurs through:\\n- **report_selection_error()** (fulfillment_errors.rs:57-100): Main entry point for reporting trait errors\\n- **report_extra_impl_obligation()**: Reports obligations from impl items\\n- **on_unimplemented**: Custom error messages from #[diagnostic] attributes\\n- **suggestions**: Helpful suggestions for fixing trait errors\\n\\n### The Obligation Chain Flow\\n\\n1. **Registration**: Obligations registered via `ObligationCtxt.register_obligation()` → `TraitEngine.register_predicate_obligation()` → added to `FulfillmentContext.predicates` (ObligationForest)\\n\\n2. **Processing**: `FulfillmentContext.select()` calls `predicates.process_obligations(&mut FulfillProcessor)`\\n\\n3. **Obligation Processing**: `FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()` is called for each pending obligation\\n   - Checks if obligation needs processing via `needs_process_obligation()`\\n   - Calls `SelectionContext.select(obligation)`\\n\\n4. **Selection**: `SelectionContext.select()` → `candidate_from_obligation()` → `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`\\n   - Checks cache, calls `assemble_candidates()` to collect candidate implementations\\n   - Evaluates each candidate with `evaluate_candidate()`\\n   - Selects the best candidate (if any)\\n\\n5. **Confirmation**: Selected candidate is confirmed with `confirm_candidate()`\\n   - Unifies types and generates nested obligations\\n   - Returns `Selection` (impl source)\\n\\n6. **Result Processing**: `ProcessResult` returned to forest\\n   - `Changed(subobligations)`: Sub-obligations added to forest, parent suspended\\n   - `Unchanged`: Obligation stays pending for next iteration\\n   - `Error`: Obligation marked as error, backtrace recorded\\n\\n7. **Completion**: When all obligations resolved or errors detected, `process_obligations()` returns `Outcome` with completed obligations and errors\\n\\n8. **Error Reporting**: `report_selection_error()` called for unresolved errors, generating user-facing diagnostics\\n\\n### New Trait Solver\\n\\nIn parallel, the new trait solver (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/) provides a modern implementation:\\n- Uses `FulfillmentCtxt` (different from old `FulfillmentContext`)\\n- Implements goal-based solving rather than obligation forest\\n- Used when `InferCtxt.next_trait_solver()` returns true\\n- Can be enabled with `-Znext-solver` flag\\n- Accessed through `InferCtxtSelectExt::select_in_new_trait_solver()`\\n\\nBoth solvers maintain the same public API through the `TraitEngine` trait, allowing for gradual migration.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2020,"cache_read_input_tokens":87449,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2020},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"48cda48c-3bb5-4bc4-b7f3-99537387eefa","uuid":"77d9a8ed-50b2-47b9-95e3-fe3a6a625dd8"}

**ObligationForest** data structure, which manages the forest of pending trait obligations. The chain represents the old (traditional) trait solver architecture, with a modern new solver implementation alongside it.\\n\\n### Core Components\\n\\n#### 1. ObligationForest (rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)\\nThe **ObligationForest** is the fundamental data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It:\\n- Maintains a forest of obligation nodes, each with state (Pending, Waiting, Success, Error)\\n- Implements obligation dependency tracking with parent-child relationships\\n- Processes obligations via the `ObligationProcessor` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:268)\\n- Returns outcomes containing completed obligations and errors\\n- Caches processed results to avoid duplicate work\\n\\nThe forest uses three core result types defined by `ProcessResult<O, E>`:\\n- `Unchanged`: Ambiguous result, obligation stalled on type inference\\n- `Changed(Vec<O>)`: Obligation satisfied with subobligations\\n- `Error(E)`: Obligation failed\\n\\n#### 2. FulfillmentContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:61-104)\\nThe **FulfillmentContext** is the old trait solver's main context that manages trait fulfillment:\\n- Wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implements the `TraitEngine` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs:136)\\n- Registers obligations via `register_predicate_obligation()`\\n- Processes obligations through the `select()` method which invokes `FulfillProcessor`\\n- Snapshot-aware to ensure correct context usage\\n\\n#### 3. FulfillProcessor (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:252-450)\\nThe **FulfillProcessor** implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait and:\\n- Processes each obligation in the forest by invoking trait selection\\n- Implements `needs_process_obligation()` with optimizations checking stalled inference variables\\n- Calls `SelectionContext.select()` for each obligation\\n- Generates sub-obligations from confirmed candidates\\n- Converts solver errors to fulfillment errors\\n\\n#### 4. SelectionContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs:104-126)\\nThe **SelectionContext** is the central context for trait candidate selection:\\n- Maintains inference context and freshener for trait predicates\\n- Tracks intercrate ambiguity causes for coherence checking\\n- Implements the selection algorithm via `select()` and `candidate_from_obligation()`\\n- Manages trait obligation stacks to detect cycles\\n- Caches selection results for performance\\n\\n#### 5. Candidate Assembly (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs:25-100)\\nThe **assemble_candidates()** method:\\n- Collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation\\n- Sources candidates from:\\n  - Trait aliases\\n  - User-defined impl blocks\\n  - Where-clause bounds\\n  - Built-in traits (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n  - Projection predicates\\n- Returns a `SelectionCandidateSet` with definite and ambiguous candidates\\n\\n#### 6. Confirmation (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs:32-100)\\nThe **confirm_candidate()** method:\\n- Verifies that a selected candidate actually applies to the obligation\\n- Unifies trait reference type parameters\\n- Generates nested obligations based on the candidate type:\\n  - `ImplCandidate`: Calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` to generate where-clause obligations\\n  - `ParamCandidate`: Generates obligations from where-clause bounds\\n  - `BuiltinCandidate`: No nested obligations\\n  - `ObjectCandidate`, `ClosureCandidate`, etc.: Generate type-specific obligations\\n- Returns an `ImplSource` representing the selected implementation\\n\\n#### 7. Impl Matching (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs:24-117)\\nThe **MatchAgainstFreshVars** structure:\\n- Implements the `TypeRelation` trait to match types against fresh type variables\\n- Used to check if an impl's trait reference matches an obligation\\n- Approximates whether unification would succeed\\n- Returns Ok if match succeeds, Err if it fails\\n\\n#### 8. TraitEngine & ObligationCtxt (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs)\\nThe **TraitEngine** trait defines:\\n- `register_predicate_obligation()`: Adds obligations to the engine\\n- `try_evaluate_obligations()`: Processes pending obligations\\n- `report_fulfillment_errors()`: Reports errors for unfulfilled obligations\\n\\nThe **ObligationCtxt** provides a simpler API wrapper around TraitEngine.\\n\\n#### 9. Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/)\\nError reporting occurs through:\\n- **report_selection_error()** (fulfillment_errors.rs:57-100): Main entry point for reporting trait errors\\n- **report_extra_impl_obligation()**: Reports obligations from impl items\\n- **on_unimplemented**: Custom error messages from #[diagnostic] attributes\\n- **suggestions**: Helpful suggestions for fixing trait errors\\n\\n### The Obligation Chain Flow\\n\\n1. **Registration**: Obligations registered via `ObligationCtxt.register_obligation()` → `TraitEngine.register_predicate_obligation()` → added to `FulfillmentContext.predicates` (ObligationForest)\\n\\n2. **Processing**: `FulfillmentContext.select()` calls `predicates.process_obligations(&mut FulfillProcessor)`\\n\\n3. **Obligation Processing**: `FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()` is called for each pending obligation\\n   - Checks if obligation needs processing via `needs_process_obligation()`\\n   - Calls `SelectionContext.select(obligation)`\\n\\n4. **Selection**: `SelectionContext.select()` → `candidate_from_obligation()` → `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`\\n   - Checks cache, calls `assemble_candidates()` to collect candidate implementations\\n   - Evaluates each candidate with `evaluate_candidate()`\\n   - Selects the best candidate (if any)\\n\\n5. **Confirmation**: Selected candidate is confirmed with `confirm_candidate()`\\n   - Unifies types and generates nested obligations\\n   - Returns `Selection` (impl source)\\n\\n6. **Result Processing**: `ProcessResult` returned to forest\\n   - `Changed(subobligations)`: Sub-obligations added to forest, parent suspended\\n   - `Unchanged`: Obligation stays pending for next iteration\\n   - `Error`: Obligation marked as error, backtrace recorded\\n\\n7. **Completion**: When all obligations resolved or errors detected, `process_obligations()` returns `Outcome` with completed obligations and errors\\n\\n8. **Error Reporting**: `report_selection_error()` called for unresolved errors, generating user-facing diagnostics\\n\\n### New Trait Solver\\n\\nIn parallel, the new trait solver (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/) provides a modern implementation:\\n- Uses `FulfillmentCtxt` (different from old `FulfillmentContext`)\\n- Implements goal-based solving rather than obligation forest\\n- Used when `InferCtxt.next_trait_solver()` returns true\\n- Can be enabled with `-Znext-solver` flag\\n- Accessed through `InferCtxtSelectExt::select_in_new_trait_solver()`\\n\\nBoth solvers maintain the same public API through the `TraitEngine` trait, allowing for gradual migration.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
